в—Ҹ Fractionation optimization plan вҖ” review before implementation

  What's actually allocating per fractionation call

  Walked the call tree from make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop. The threaded
  marker loop itself (lines 110-125 of Fractionation.jl) is clean вҖ”
  transform_marker_to_magma is pure in-place writes, linear_interp_bisection is
  pure scalar return. The cost is outside the marker loop, in the per-timestep
  setup work that builds the moho and partial-melt surfaces.

  Per call, the chain allocates roughly in this order of severity:

  #: 1
  Allocation: marker_indices_layer_tmp = Vector{Int64}(undef, marknum)

    could be 200вҖ“400 MB per call

  Where: calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt (TopAndBottom.jl:125-126)
  Size: 2 Г— toponum Г— 8 B per call (small)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 4
  Allocation: y_surface_smooth = Vector{Float64}(undef, xnum)
  Where: smooth_surface (SmoothSurface.jl:24)
  Size: toponum Г— 8 B per call, called ~3Г— per fractionation
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 5
  Allocation: topo_gridx = gridt[1, :] etc.
  Where: Fractionation.jl:85, 86, 141, 142; Drainage.jl:110, 111
  Size: toponum Г— 8 B Г— 6 slicings
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 6
  Allocation: min.(moho_gridy, partial_melt_gridy)
  Where: Fractionation.jl:106
  Size: toponum Г— 8 B (broadcast result)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 7
  Allocation: vcat(...) for material id lists
  Where: Fractionation.jl:190, 200
  Size: tiny

  Item #1 dominates and is consistent with the 477 MB/call delta. With marknum
  likely in the tens of millions for case4 by step 1216+, allocating and
  discarding a Vector{Int64} of that size per fractionation call is exactly the
  kind of allocator pressure that on 96 threads causes the heap to grow well
  beyond the per-call size.

  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt is called twice per fractionation:
  - once via calculate_oceanic_moho for the gabbroic crust matids (~7 matids)
  - once via calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain for
  UltramaficMantlePartiallyMolten

  So item #1 fires twice per fractionation = ~80вҖ“800 MB transient (depending on
  marknum) per fractionation call.

  Plan

  Tier A вҖ” kill the per-call marknum allocation

  This is the bulk of the win. Two-step preallocation mirroring the pattern you
  already used for partial_melt_marker_indices in model.melting.arrays.buffers.

  A.1 вҖ” add a structure-buffers group

  Add a new field group model.markers.arrays.structure (or extend the existing
  model.melting.arrays.buffers if it semantically fits вҖ” but melting and
  structure are different concerns, so I'd lean toward a new group) containing:

  mutable struct StructureBuffers <: AbstractArrayGroup
      marker_indices_layer_tmp::MarkerArrayInt1DState{Int64}   # size marknum, 
  scratch
      marker_indices_layer::MarkerArrayInt1DState{Int64}        # size marknum, 
  packed-prefix output
  end

  Both sized to marknum at construction вҖ” same convention as
  partial_melt_marker_indices (filled valid in [1:count], tail is stale).

  A.2 вҖ” change filter_markers_outside_of_layer to use buffers + return a count

  Current signature returns a freshly-sized Vector{Int64}. New signature:

  function filter_markers_outside_of_layer!(
      marker_indices_layer::Vector{Int64},            # preallocated, size 
  marknum
      marker_indices_layer_tmp::Vector{Int64},        # preallocated, size 
  marknum
      marker_matid::Vector{Int16},
      material_ids_of_layer::Vector{Int16}
  )::Int  # returns icount

  Caller responsibility: pass in the buffers, use [1:icount] view for downstream
   consumption.

  A.3 вҖ” propagate through calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt

  This function also needs to accept the buffers (or accept the model directly).
   Its signature already has 6 positional args plus 2 keyword args; I'd lean
  toward adding an optional model keyword that, when provided, sources buffers
  from it; otherwise falls back to the current allocation behavior. This way
  existing callers (which I enumerated below) don't break.

  Callers of calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt (8 call sites):
  - Fractionation.jl:151 (oceanic_moho) вҖ” fix as part of fractionation work
  - Fractionation.jl:179 (calculate_moho вҖ” appears UNUSED in this code path;
  verify)
  - Drainage.jl:130 (partial_melt domain) вҖ” fix
  - structure/ModelStructureManager.jl:217 вҖ” fix if hot
  - structure/utils/TopoFromMarkers.jl:56, 63 вҖ” fix if hot
  - structure/utils/TopAndBottom.jl:33 (internal call from
  calculate_layer_thickness) вҖ” fix
  - The calculate_top_and_bottom_of_swarm_opt variant in compaction is a
  separate path; not needed for fractionation but same pattern would help
  sediment transport.

  The drainage call site is in your fractionation hot path so that one is
  required. The others can be migrated incrementally вҖ” passing model=nothing
  keeps the old behavior for callers we don't migrate yet.

  Expected impact: eliminates 200вҖ“400 MB per fractionation call. Should drop the
   section's per-call delta to roughly the size of the remaining (xnum-scale)
  allocations вҖ” order of magnitude smaller.

  Tier B вҖ” eliminate the xnum-scale allocators

  Once Tier A lands, items #3, #4, #5, #6 above remain. Each is small (toponum Г—
   8 B), but they fire multiple times per fractionation and are exactly the kind
   of allocations that under high GC pressure aggregate into noticeable maxrss
  bumps.

  B.1 вҖ” preallocate tops/bottoms buffers

  Add to topography arrays (or a new fractionation buffers group):
  - top_buffer::TopoArray1DState (size toponum)
  - bottom_buffer::TopoArray1DState (size toponum)

  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt becomes a ! function writing into these.
   Important: these need to be added to initialize_topo_arrays! alongside
  compaction_array (the function we just fixed) so they're resized on toponum
  changes.

  B.2 вҖ” smooth_surface! in-place variant

  Convert smooth_surface to smooth_surface!(out::Vector{Float64}, 
  ytopo::Vector{Float64}; nsmooth)::Nothing. Note the algorithm reads each input
   element with offsets from i, so out and ytopo must be different arrays вҖ”
  caller has to allocate or reuse a separate buffer.

  Add a smoothed_surface_buffer::TopoArray1DState to topography arrays (same
  lifecycle as B.1) and have the caller pass it.

  Or вҖ” cheaper alternative вҖ” leave smooth_surface returning a fresh array, but
  reduce the number of calls. Currently fractionation invokes it 2Г— and drainage
   1Г—. If we accept the small allocation it's not really the issue; Tier A is
  what matters.

  B.3 вҖ” eliminate gridt[N, :] slicing

  Replace topo_gridx = gridt[1, :] with topo_gridx = view(gridt, 1, :)
  everywhere it's read-only. Verify no callers mutate. (Quick check: most uses I
   see pass it to functions that read indices, not write вҖ” but worth confirming
  during the edit.)

  B.4 вҖ” in-place min.(...)

  Fractionation.jl:106: change moho_gridy = min.(moho_gridy, partial_melt_gridy)
   to moho_gridy .= min.(moho_gridy, partial_melt_gridy). One-character change.

  Tier C вҖ” verify and cleanup (no perf change expected)

  C.1 вҖ” confirm calculate_moho is unused
  Fractionation.jl:167 defines calculate_moho (with the bug-prone
  get_matids_mantle allocator at line 188). Check whether it's called anywhere;
  I didn't see it in my search. If unused, delete to prevent future confusion.

  C.2 вҖ” verify transform_marker_to_magma allocation-free
  Already done via inspection вҖ” pure in-place writes (MagmaBody.jl:454-485).

  C.3 вҖ” verify linear_interp_bisection allocation-free
  Already done вҖ” pure scalar return (MathTools.jl:201-217).

  Risk assessment

  Recommended sequence

  1. Tier A as one PR вҖ” A.1 + A.2 + A.3 together, since they form a single
  logical change (preallocate buffers, propagate signature). For A.3, only touch
   the fractionation/drainage call sites first; leave the structure/topo callers
   using the old fallback path. This bounds the change set.
  2. Measure after Tier A вҖ” if fractionation's per-call delta drops to <100 MB,
  Tier B is optional.
  3. Tier B if needed вҖ” quick sweeps once we know the residual cost.
  4. Tier C вҖ” anytime; just hygiene.

  Open question for you

  Should I follow your BuffersGroup convention and put the new buffers under
  model.markers.arrays.structure (new field), or extend the existing
  model.melting.arrays.buffers (semantically a stretch since
  structure-of-marker-layer-finding isn't melting)? My lean is a new group вҖ”
  keeps domains separated вҖ” but you have stronger feel for the codebase's
  organization conventions.

  Ready for your call on whether to proceed and where to land the new buffers.

вқҜ Could you evaluate the work that you just did? For example, why did you pass

  вҺҝ В в§ү Selected 1 lines from src/melt_model/fractionation/Fractionation.jl in Cursor

в—Ҹ Good prompt вҖ” let me critique honestly.

  The model keyword choice вҖ” your prompt highlights the weakest part

  I passed model::Union{ModelData, Nothing} as a keyword down through
  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt. The cleaner design would have been to 
  pass the buffer itself.

  What I did:
  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt(
      ..., model=model
  )

  What I should have considered:
  buffer = model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array
  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt(
      ..., layer_index_buffer=buffer
  )

  Why the buffer-based design is better:

  1. Coupling. TopAndBottom.jl lives in src/structure/utils/ вҖ” it's a low-level
  utility consumed by structure-finding code, melt extraction, drainage,
  sediment compaction, topography construction. By making it take model, I baked
   model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array вҖ” a specific path
  through the model object вҖ” into a generic utility. If someone reorganizes that
   field (e.g., moves it to a different group), every utility caller breaks for
  a layout reason rather than a semantic reason.
  2. Testability. Passing a buffer means I can unit-test
  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt with any Vector{Int64} of sufficient
  size. With model, I'd need to construct a full ModelData to exercise the fast
  path вҖ” exactly what we just hit when running the integration test.
  3. The "I followed the existing pattern" defense is weak. Yes, the recent
  buffer-reuse work in MagmaBody and PartialMeltIndices takes model::ModelData
  and looks up buffers internally. But those modules are part of the melt domain
   вҖ” they live next to the buffers they use. TopAndBottom is shared
  infrastructure, where the model-path coupling is more out of place.

  I should have flagged this design choice in the plan and asked. The
  buffer-based approach is a small refactor away (just one signature change and
  updating two call sites), and worth doing now while the code is fresh.

  Other things worth critiquing

  The dual API I left behind.
  After my changes, filter_markers_outside_of_layer (allocating) is only ever
  called from inside calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt's fallback branch.
  It's no longer a public surface anyone needs. I could have inlined the 3-line
  allocate-then-call sequence into the else-branch and deleted the wrapper.
  Keeping it as a separate function adds a name in the namespace for no real
  benefit.

  The Union{ModelData, Nothing}=nothing pattern is silent on misuse.
  If a future caller forgets model=model, they get the legacy allocating path
  with no warning. There's nothing in the type system or function name that
  signals "you should be passing model". A Vector{Int64} buffer keyword would
  have the same risk in principle, but layer_index_buffer reads more obviously
  like "you need to provide this for performance".

  The @assert adds runtime cost on every call.
  I wrote @assert length(marker_indices_layer) >= marknum inside
  filter_markers_outside_of_layer!. It's one comparison, so the overhead is
  negligible вҖ” but @assert runs unconditionally in Julia. I could have used
  @boundscheck (elided when --check-bounds=no) or just relied on the bounds
  check that Julia inserts on the indexed write itself. Mild stylistic issue.

  The Structure group with one field is borderline.
  For Tier A only, there's a single buffer. If Tier B never adds more buffers to
   it, this group is overhead вҖ” a separate file, separate import, separate
  constructor вҖ” for one array. Defensible because: the existing BuffersGroup (5
  fields) is melt-specific and this isn't melt-related, and "structure-finding
  scratch buffers" is a reasonable bucket that future Tier B additions would
  extend. But if Tier B doesn't materialize, this looks oversized.

  What I think I got right

  - Functional equivalence verified end-to-end. Both my synthetic test and the
  existing MeltDrainageDividesTest reproduce identical outputs. Worth more than
  the design tidiness questions.
  - Backward compatibility preserved. Non-migrated callers compile and run
  unchanged. No silent semantic breaks.
  - Backup compatibility handled. New buffer field gracefully degrades on old
  backups via the same "No data found in jld file" path that already exists for
  the other recent buffer additions.
  - The ! variant follows Julia convention (mutating function, returns count,
  packed-prefix output).
  - Pattern matches the existing Advection and Buffers groups for the
  array-registration / group-include / collection-wiring boilerplate.
  - Leaving the other 4 callers on the legacy path is correct for the stated
  scope вҖ” it bounds the change and makes the impact measurable. Migrating them
  in the same PR would have made it harder to attribute any downstream issues.

  Recommendation

  The model-coupling issue is worth fixing before you ship this. It's a small
  refactor:
  - model::Union{ModelData, Nothing}=nothing вҶ’
  layer_index_buffer::Union{Vector{Int64}, Nothing}=nothing
  - Two call sites do the lookup in the caller (buf = 
  model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array; ..., 
  layer_index_buffer=buf)
  - TopAndBottom.jl no longer needs to dot-into model layout

  Want me to apply that refactor? It's a low-risk follow-up that improves the
  design without changing behavior.

вқҜ Help me understand the change you just made.                                  
  вҺҝ В в§ү Selected 1 lines from src/melt_model/fractionation/Fractionation.jl in Cursor

в—Ҹ Sure. Walking through it from your selected line 96 outward.

  The hot path that triggered the work

  Every timestep, make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop calls
  calculate_oceanic_moho(model) at Fractionation.jl:97 (which is the function
  you've selected, defined at line 96). Inside that function, line 152 calls
  down to calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt(...), which used to allocate a
  fresh Vector{Int64} of size marknum (the total number of markers) every single
   time. With marknum in the tens of millions, that's hundreds of MB allocated
  and discarded per call.

  The fix has two halves: provide a place to put a reusable buffer (data side),
  and teach the function to use it (control side).

  Data side вҖ” adding a persistent buffer to the model

  A model state value
  (model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array) doesn't appear out
   of nowhere. EarthBox builds those nested fields up through several layers of
  struct definitions, and each layer has to know about the new field.

  That's why there are five files for what feels like "add one array":

  File: src/data_types/arrays/core/ArrayRegistry.jl
  Role: Central registry of every named array in the model. Gives
    marker_indices_layer a name, units, type, and description. The field's
    metadata lives here.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  File: src/model_data/markers/arrays/groups/StructureGroup.jl
  Role: New file. Defines a Structure group вҖ” a small struct that owns the
    marker_indices_layer field and knows how to construct it sized to marknum.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  File: src/model_data/markers/arrays/groups/__init__.jl
  Role: Tells the package to compile the new group file.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  File: src/model_data/markers/arrays/ArrayCollection.jl
  Role: The marker arrays collection вҖ” the thing exposed as
  model.markers.arrays.
    I added structure::Structure as a new field and the Structure(marknum) call
    to its constructor.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  File: (no fifth вҖ” that's it for the data side)
  Role:

  So model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array is now a
  Vector{Int64} of length marknum that lives for the whole run, allocated once
  at model construction and reused across timesteps.

  The reason it lives in a Structure group rather than alongside Advection or
  Buffers is that this buffer is consumed by structure-finding utilities
  (top/bottom of layer, drainage, fractionation, topography) вҖ” not by velocity
  advection or melt-extraction internals. Keeps the domain separation clean.

  Control side вҖ” teaching the function to use the buffer

  src/structure/utils/TopAndBottom.jl has two related changes:

  1. A new function, filter_markers_outside_of_layer!(buf, marker_matid, 
  material_ids_of_layer). The exclamation mark is Julia convention for "this
  function mutates one of its arguments." It takes a pre-allocated buf, fills
  positions [1:icount] with the marker indices that belong to the queried layer
  (in original marker order), and returns icount вҖ” the number of valid
  positions. The buffer's tail is left in an unspecified state because consumers
   are supposed to bound their loops by the returned count.
  2. calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt got a new keyword argument:
  model::Union{ModelData, Nothing}=nothing. Inside the function, there's a
  branch:
    - If model was passed in, use the persistent buffer at
  model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array and call
  filter_markers_outside_of_layer! on it. No allocation.
    - If model is nothing (the default), fall back to the old
  filter_markers_outside_of_layer (allocating) for backward compatibility with
  all the other callers I didn't migrate.

  The body of the function past that branch is identical to before вҖ” same
  Threads.@threads loop over grid columns, same scoring of which markers fall in
   each column's search radius. The only thing that changed is where the index 
  list it iterates over comes from.

  The old filter_markers_outside_of_layer function still exists; I refactored
  its body to internally call the new ! variant on a freshly-allocated vector.
  Same external behavior, less code duplication.

  The two call-site changes

  Now we just need to flip the switch on the two hot callers вҖ”
  calculate_oceanic_moho and calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain:

  - Fractionation.jl:152 (inside calculate_oceanic_moho): added model=model to
  the calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt call. Since calculate_oceanic_moho
  already had model::ModelData as its first argument, the local variable model
  was already in scope вҖ” I just needed to forward it as the keyword.
  - Drainage.jl:130 (inside calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain): same
  pattern. That function already had model in scope; added model=model to the
  call.

  End-to-end, on a fractionation timestep:

  1. make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop calls calculate_oceanic_moho(model).
  2. calculate_oceanic_moho calls calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt(..., 
  model=model).
  3. Inside, the model !== nothing branch triggers.
  4. It pulls model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array вҖ” the
  same persistent buffer used last timestep, last hour, since startup.
  5. filter_markers_outside_of_layer! walks all markers, packs the
  gabbroic-crust ones into the front of the buffer, returns the count.
  6. The threaded grid-column loop runs as before, but reading from the
  persistent buffer instead of a freshly-minted vector.
  7. Function returns; buffer is left "dirty" but that's fine вҖ” next call will
  overwrite it from positionВ 1.

  No allocation occurred. Same (tops, bottoms) returned. Bit-for-bit identical
  output, verified by the drainage-divides integration test reproducing the
  expected [0.0, 18000.0, ..., 500000.0].

  What didn't change

  - Everywhere else that calls calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt вҖ”
  calculate_layer_thickness in TopAndBottom.jl itself, callers in
  structure/utils/TopoFromMarkers.jl, the unused calculate_moho in
  Fractionation.jl вҖ” runs the legacy allocating path because they don't pass
  model. They behave exactly as they did before.
  - The transform_marker_to_magma function called per-marker inside the threaded
   loop wasn't touched; it was already allocation-free.
  - The smaller per-call allocations (the tops, bottoms, smooth_surface outputs
  at xnum scale) weren't addressed вҖ” those are Tier B if profiling shows they
  matter.

  That's the change in full. The "hard part" was the data side (5 files of
  plumbing for a new field) and the design choice on the control side (model
  keyword vs. buffer keyword вҖ” which I criticized in the previous response).

вң» SautГ©ed for 44s

вҖ» recap: We're cutting RAM growth in EarthBox case4 on the 96-core machine; Tier A is implemented and tested, eliminating the per-call marknum-sized allocation in fractionation and drainage. Next: launch the case4 restart and watch fractionation's per-call delta.

  What changed for these callers

  Behaviorally: nothing. The fallback branch (model === nothing) calls
  filter_markers_outside_of_layer (the legacy non-! function), which still
  returns a freshly-allocated Vector{Int64} of length icount containing the
  matching marker indices in original-marker order. Same return type, same
  values, same ordering. The integration test (MeltDrainageDividesTest) confirms
   bit-for-bit equivalence.

  Implementation-wise: a small simplification. I refactored the body of legacy
  filter_markers_outside_of_layer to internally call the new ! variant + resize!
   rather than keep its original two-buffer + parallel-copy implementation. Both
   produce the same output, but:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

  в”Ӯ               в”Ӯ tmpвҶ’final                   в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  So non-migrated callers get a side benefit they didn't ask for: one fewer
  allocation per call, and they skip the (probably-unhelpful) parallel copy step
   that wasn't worth threading anyway. Net effect: marginally less allocation 
  pressure on non-fractionation paths, no behavior change.

  What's added persistently to the model state

  model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array is a Vector{Int64}
  sized to marknum that now exists for every model, regardless of whether
  fractionation runs. Memory cost:

  - 10M markers вҶ’ +80 MB persistent
  - 50M markers вҶ’ +400 MB persistent

  This is a permanent floor increase even for runs that don't exercise
  fractionation or drainage. For case4 it's clearly worth it (you save several
  hundred MB of transient allocation per timestep). For a hypothetical model
  without fractionation, it's pure overhead вҖ” modest but real.

  What changed for backup files

  The marker_indices_layer field gets picked up by reflection (fieldnames walks
  the new Structure group automatically), so it's added to:

  1. The obj_dict used for both saving and loading backups.
  2. JLD2 backup files written by the new code (size grows by marknum Г— 8 B).

  Cross-version compatibility:
  - New code вҶ’ old backup: prints "No data found in jld file for
  marker_indices_layer" warning during load, constructor's zeroed buffer is
  preserved. Works correctly because the buffer gets overwritten on first call.
  (You already saw this pattern with the other recent buffer additions.)
  - Old code вҶ’ new backup: untested, but JLD2's read path will see an unknown
  key and ignore it. Should work; not a workflow you'd normally run.

  What changed for ModelInfo / introspection

  src/model_manager/info/ModelInfo.jl walks the model via propertynames. The new
   structure group will show up in any model-summary output you produce. Not a
  bug вҖ” just one new line listing marker_indices_layer in info dumps. If you
  have any tests that match exact ModelInfo output strings, they'd need
  updating; I didn't see any.

  What was untouched

  These functions and their callers are completely unaffected:

  - calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer (the non-_opt version, TopAndBottom.jl:54)
   вҖ” separate function, still allocates as before. Used by some legacy paths.
  - calculate_top_and_bottom_of_swarm_opt (TopAndBottom.jl:205) вҖ” used by
  sediment-transport compaction; no changes here.
  - calculate_top_and_bottom_of_swarm (TopAndBottom.jl:261) вҖ” same.
  - transform_marker_to_magma, linear_interp_bisection вҖ” pure functions, already
   allocation-free, not modified.
  - All threading parameters, all numerical results.

  The risk to non-fractionation code is minimal because: (a) the integration

в—Ҹ You're correct, and I owe you an accurate picture. Let me trace this properly.

  The two callers of calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain

  Fractionation.jl:102  вҶ’  inside make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop
  Drainage.jl:14        вҶ’  inside calculate_melt_drainage_divides!

  Because I modified calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain itself (not
  just one of its call sites) to pass model=model down, both callers now 
  automatically use the buffer path. The function has no model::Union{ModelData,
   Nothing}=nothing keyword вҖ” it always forwards the model it already has. So
  every caller is migrated implicitly.

  What that means in practice

  calculate_melt_drainage_divides! (Drainage.jl:9) is called from outside
  fractionation as part of the per-extraction drainage analysis. In the pre-fix
  log, that path showed up as a separate section:

  в–Һ Finished calculating melt drainage divides: +1.6 GB across 9 calls, 195 
  в–Һ MB/call

  That section was attributed cleanly to drainage, not fractionation. After this
   change, that section's per-call delta should also drop вҖ” because the
  underlying calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain вҶ’
  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt вҶ’ filter_markers_outside_of_layer! chain
   is now buffer-using regardless of which entry point invoked it.

  So my "Tier A" change has a wider impact than I claimed:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Both fractionation and drainage benefit from the same single fix.

  Is the shared buffer safe across these two consumers?

  Yes:

  - The time loop is sequential. Fractionation and drainage don't execute
  concurrently.
  - Each call to filter_markers_outside_of_layer! overwrites the buffer from
  position 1, ignoring whatever was left from the previous caller. No stale data
   leaks between consumers.
  - Inside any single call, the threaded for j in 1:xnum reads from the buffer
  after filter_markers_outside_of_layer! has finished writing вҖ” no read/write
  race.

  Where my prior answer was wrong

  I said:

  в–Һ "These five call sites still use the legacy allocating path"
  в–Һ ... and listed Drainage.jl:130 as among the "non-fractionation callers" вҖ” 
  в–Һ but that was about the internal calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt call 
  в–Һ site, which IS migrated.

  What I should have said is that the migration applies at the
  calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain boundary, which means the
  optimization propagates to every caller of that function вҖ” fractionation and
  drainage divides. The five truly-unmigrated call sites are only the ones that
  call calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt directly without going through
  Drainage or Fractionation:

  src/structure/utils/TopAndBottom.jl:33      вҖ” calculate_layer_thickness
  src/structure/ModelStructureManager.jl:217  вҖ” initial structure construction
  src/structure/utils/TopoFromMarkers.jl:56   вҖ”
  calculate_topography_from_markers
  src/structure/utils/TopoFromMarkers.jl:63   вҖ” same module
  src/melt_model/fractionation/Fractionation.jl:179 вҖ” calculate_moho (dead code)

  Those five still use the legacy allocating path. Everything else вҖ”
  fractionation, drainage divides, partial-melt-domain calculation regardless of
   caller вҖ” uses the buffer.

  This makes the change a bigger win than I originally framed it. Thanks for
  catching it.

   baseline; offset against the per-step transient savings.

  3. Why the new code produces identical results

  Argument 1 вҖ” filter_markers_outside_of_layer! is bitwise equivalent to its 
  predecessor's output

  Old function:
  1. Allocate tmp[marknum]
  2. For imarker in 1:marknum:
     - if matid in layer: tmp[icount+1] = imarker; icount += 1
     - else: tmp[imarker] = -1   вҶҗ functionally meaningless write (overwritten)
  3. Allocate out[icount]
  4. Parallel-copy tmp[1..icount] вҶ’ out[1..icount]
  5. Return out

  New function (buffer variant):
  1. Use provided buf (size вүҘ marknum)
  2. For imarker in 1:marknum:
     - if matid in layer: icount += 1; buf[icount] = imarker
  3. Return icount

  Equivalence:
  - The old function's output is a length-icount vector with values [matching 
  imarker in original-marker order].
  - The new function leaves positions [1..icount] of buf containing exactly the 
  same values in the same order (the loop is serial in both, identical iteration
   order).
  - The old function's else-branch -1 writes never affect output вҖ” those
  positions are either overwritten by a later matching iteration or never read
  by stepВ 4.
  - The parallel copy in step 4 is byte-for-byte equivalent to a serial copy of
  the same range.

  Therefore, for any input (marker_matid, material_ids_of_layer), the new
  function's buf[1:icount] вүЎ the old function's returned vector.

  Argument 2 вҖ” refactored legacy filter_markers_outside_of_layer is bitwise 
  equivalent

  function filter_markers_outside_of_layer(marker_matid, material_ids_of_layer)
      marknum = length(marker_matid)
      buf = Vector{Int64}(undef, marknum)
      icount = filter_markers_outside_of_layer!(buf, marker_matid,
  material_ids_of_layer)
      return resize!(buf, icount)
  end

  By the previous argument, buf[1:icount] is bit-equivalent to the original
  returned vector. resize!(buf, icount) truncates buf to length icount in place
  (no reallocation, no value change). The returned vector therefore has the same
   length and the same values as the original implementation.

  Argument 3 вҖ” calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt is unchanged below the 
  filter call

  Both branches of the new if model !== nothing / else produce two identifiers
  after the branch:
  - marker_indices_layer: a Vector{Int64} whose first marknum_layer entries are
  the matching marker indices in original order.
  - marknum_layer: the count icount.

  The downstream code is literally byte-for-byte unchanged:
  for imarker_layer in 1:marknum_layer
      imarker = marker_indices_layer[imarker_layer]
      ...
  end

  Both paths produce the same first marknum_layer index values. The buffer-path
  tail (positions [marknum_layer+1:end]) is never read. Same downstream
  computation, same tops and bottoms outputs.

  Argument 4 вҖ” calculate_oceanic_moho and 
  calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain are unchanged except for the 
  keyword forwarded

  Both functions added exactly one keyword model=model to their inner call. By
  argument 3, that produces the same outputs from the inner call. Every line
  surrounding the call is unchanged. Therefore both wrappers produce identical
  outputs.

  Argument 5 вҖ” empirical verification

  - Direct equivalence test, small input: legacy and buffer paths produce
  identical [1, 3, 4, 7, 8].
  - Stress test, 1M markers: identical 199,735-element output vectors.
  - Integration test (MeltDrainageDividesTest): produces the exact expected
  drainage divides
  [0.0, 18000.0, 84750.0, 150250.0, 215500.0, 281750.0,
   348750.0, 416000.0, 483500.0, 500000.0]
  - bit-for-bit. This test exercises the migrated
  calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain end-to-end.

  callers first as a bounded change and defer the rest. Those deferred call
  sites still allocate a marknum-sized vector per call:

  Used by: calculate_layer_thickness

  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Call site: src/structure/utils/TopoFromMarkers.jl:56

  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  There's also calculate_top_and_bottom_of_swarm_opt (the swarm variant of the
  layer function), used by sediment-transport compaction. Same allocation
  pattern, same fix would apply. Not strictly Tier A since it's a different
  function, but the same mechanical refactor.

  Design improvement I flagged in my self-review

  The model::Union{ModelData, Nothing} keyword approach couples a structural
  utility to model layout. The cleaner alternative is to pass the buffer
  directly:

  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt(...; layer_index_buffer=buf)

  with callers doing the lookup themselves. Same numerical behavior, better
  separation of concerns. You haven't approved this refactor yet; flagging it
  here for the record. Low-risk follow-up.

  Strict answer to your question

  If "Tier A" means "kill the marknum-sized allocation in
  filter_markers_outside_of_layer":
  - For the fractionation and drainage paths: complete.
  - For the 5 other call sites: not yet migrated (deferred per the original
  plan, but mechanically the same fix).
  - Design polish (modelвҶ’buffer): not yet applied (flagged but unapproved).

  So depending on how strictly you scope it, either Tier A is done as-planned,
  or it's two-thirds done with the most impactful third already shipped.

  1. 1M-marker correctness, no smoothing вҖ” legacy nothing-keyword path and new
  buffer-keyword path produce identical tops and bottoms vectors
  element-by-element.

  post-smooth_surface result (so the smoothing path is also unaffected).
  3. MeltDrainageDividesTest end-to-end вҖ” produces the exact expected drainage
  divides [0.0, 18000.0, 84750.0, 150250.0, 215500.0, 281750.0, 348750.0, 
  416000.0, 483500.0, 500000.0]. This test exercises the migrated
  calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain вҶ’ buffer-using path through real
  model construction.

  What this gained vs the previous design

  - TopAndBottom.jl no longer reaches into
  model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer.array. The utility takes a
   plain Vector{Int64} and doesn't know or care where it came from.
  - The import EarthBox.ModelDataContainer: ModelData in TopAndBottom.jl is
  still needed (used by calculate_layer_thickness), but the new keyword no
  longer references ModelData.
  - A future caller in a different domain (e.g., a hypothetical
  structure-finding utility outside the model object) can pass any Vector{Int64}
   they own.
  - Unit testing the function no longer requires constructing a ModelData.

  Backward compatibility

  - All 5 unmigrated callers still work вҖ” they pass no keyword, fall through the
   same way they did before.
  - Backup compatibility unchanged вҖ” the buffer field still lives in
  model.markers.arrays.structure.marker_indices_layer and gets backed up /
  loaded the same way.
  - No source-level breaking change to anyone outside the migrated callers.

  Ready for the next case4 restart.

в—Ҹ Honest item-by-item accounting against the plan you pasted:

  A.1 вҖ” structure-buffers group

  Plan said: two buffers in the group
  marker_indices_layer_tmp::MarkerArrayInt1DState{Int64}   # scratch
  marker_indices_layer::MarkerArrayInt1DState{Int64}        # packed-prefix 
  output

  What I did: one buffer
  marker_indices_layer::MarkerArrayInt1DState{Int64}

  Deviation. I dropped marker_indices_layer_tmp entirely.

  Why: When I wrote the plan I copied the original two-buffer pattern
  (marker_indices_layer_tmp + parallel copy вҶ’ final) without thinking through
  whether the tmp was actually load-bearing. When I implemented
  filter_markers_outside_of_layer!, I realized the original two-buffer/copy
  pattern was just an artifact of the old function wanting to return a
  tightly-sized Vector{Int64}. With buffer reuse, you can pack directly into the
   output buffer in a single serial pass вҖ” no tmp needed:

  icount = 0
  for imarker in 1:marknum
      if marker_matid[imarker] in material_ids_of_layer
          icount += 1
          marker_indices_layer[icount] = imarker
      end
  end

  The original parallel copy of tmp[1..icount] to a fresh output was incidental,
   not algorithmic вҖ” it didn't parallelize useful work, just moved
  already-decided data around. Skipping it is strictly cleaner. So I dropped
  half of A.1.

  This deviation is the right call but I should have flagged it explicitly
  before implementing. I didn't вҖ” that's a process miss.

  A.2 вҖ” filter_markers_outside_of_layer! signature

  Plan said:
  function filter_markers_outside_of_layer!(
      marker_indices_layer::Vector{Int64},
      marker_indices_layer_tmp::Vector{Int64},   # вҶҗ second arg
      marker_matid::Vector{Int16},
      material_ids_of_layer::Vector{Int16}
  )::Int

  What I did:
  function filter_markers_outside_of_layer!(
      marker_indices_layer::Vector{Int64},
      marker_matid::Vector{Int16},
      material_ids_of_layer::Vector{Int16}
  )::Int

  Deviation. Same root cause as A.1 вҖ” no tmp argument because no tmp buffer is
  needed. Otherwise matches the plan: takes the buffer, returns the count,
  callers use [1:icount].

  A.3 вҖ” propagate through calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt

  Plan said: "an optional model keyword that, when provided, sources buffers
  from it; otherwise falls back to the current allocation behavior."

  What I did initially: exactly that вҖ” model::Union{ModelData, Nothing}=nothing
  keyword.

  What I did after your subsequent feedback: refactored to
  layer_index_buffer::Union{Vector{Int64}, Nothing}=nothing (the cleaner
  separation we just discussed).

  Net result: the function has the optional-buffer mechanism the plan called
  for, with the bonus of decoupling from ModelData layout вҖ” better than the
  plan, achieved in two steps.

  Caller migration вҖ” what the plan listed

  The plan enumerated 8 call sites with notes on which to fix. Here's the audit:

вҖ» recap: Goal is reducing RAM growth in EarthBox; just finished Tier A fractionation/drainage buffer-reuse with the buffer-keyword refactor and verified equivalence. Next: decide whether to migrate the three deferred legacy callers or kick off the next case4 restart to measure the impact.

вқҜ I noticed that calculate_oceanic_moho is allocating topo_gridx and topo_gridy 
   after the function that calls this function does that. Can this redundency   
  be mitigated?                                                                 

в—Ҹ Good catch. Let me lay out the redundancy concretely and propose a fix.

  The redundancy

  Within one fractionation timestep, the same gridt[1, :] and gridt[2, :] slices
   are allocated 3 times:

  make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop (Fractionation.jl:85-86)
      topo_gridx = gridt[1, :]      # alloc
      topo_gridy = gridt[2, :]      # alloc
      вҶ’  calculate_oceanic_moho(model, ...)  (Fractionation.jl:141-142)
              topo_gridx = gridt[1, :]      # alloc again
              topo_gridy = gridt[2, :]      # alloc again
      вҶ’  calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain(model, ...)
  (Drainage.jl:110-111)
              topo_gridx = gridt[1, :]      # alloc again
              topo_gridy = gridt[2, :]      # alloc again

  Six Vector{Float64} allocations per fractionation call where only one of each
  is semantically needed. Each is toponum Г— 8 B (small individually, ~20вҖ“40 KB),
   but they fire every timestep on a hot path and contribute to GC churn.

  Options

  Option A вҖ” Pass topo_gridx/topo_gridy as arguments (recommended)

  Hoist the slice up to the topmost caller and pass references down.

  # In Fractionation.jl
  function calculate_oceanic_moho(
      model::ModelData,
      topo_gridx::Vector{Float64},
      topo_gridy::Vector{Float64};
      nsmooth::Int=20
  )
      # body uses topo_gridx, topo_gridy directly; gridt slice removed
  end

  # In Drainage.jl
  function calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain(
      model::ModelData,
      topo_gridx::Vector{Float64},
      topo_gridy::Vector{Float64}
  )::Vector{Float64}    # returns only top_mantle_partial_melt
      # body uses passed args; gridt slice removed
  end

  Callers to update (2 of each):
  - make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop already has topo_gridx/topo_gridy
  locally вҶ’ just pass them as positional args.
  - calculate_melt_drainage_divides! (the second caller of
  calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain) currently relies on the function
  returning topo_gridx. After the change, it allocates them itself once and
  passes them in.

  Net: 6 allocations вҶ’ 2 allocations per fractionation timestep (one each in the
   two top-level callers). Down to the irreducible minimum without reaching for
  views.

  Pros:
  - Localized change. Only 2 functions and 2 callers touched.
  - No type-signature cascade through low-level utilities
  (linear_interp_bisection, calculate_search_radius, etc. continue accepting
  concrete Vector{Float64}).
  - Keeps return types as Vector{Float64} (no SubArray propagation).
  - Matches Julia convention for "I want you to use this storage" вҖ” explicit
  positional args.

  Cons:
  - Breaks the existing return contract of
  calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain (it currently returns 3 values;
  one caller depends on that). Manageable but a real signature change.

  Option B вҖ” Use views everywhere

  topo_gridx = view(gridt, 1, :) instead of slicing. Zero allocation at the
  source, but requires consumer signatures to accept AbstractVector{Float64}
  instead of Vector{Float64}. The cascade includes:
  - linear_interp_bisection (MathTools.jl:201)
  - calculate_search_radius (TopAndBottom.jl:6)
  - calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt (TopAndBottom.jl, multiple Vector
  args)
  - All other functions that take gridx::Vector{Float64}

  Pros:
  - Truly zero allocation for these slices.
  - Applies to other call sites that allocate gridt[1, :] / gridt[2, :]
  (LavaFlowManager, RungeKutta, MarkerAdvection, CarbonateAdvect,
  UpdateSealevel, etc.) once their consumers accept AbstractVector.

  Cons:
  - Wider blast radius. Many low-level utilities need their signatures relaxed.
  - Risk of subtle dispatch changes if any caller was relying on Vector{Float64}
   specifically.
  - Views make subsequent broadcast / mutation behavior nuanced (a view shares
  storage with gridt; if any consumer mutates it, you'd corrupt the topography
  array вҖ” needs an audit).

  My recommendation

  Option A. It addresses the specific redundancy you identified with a minimal
  blast radius and is consistent with the rest of the buffer-passing pattern we
  just established for Tier A. Option B is the bigger systemic improvement but
  should be a separate, scoped refactor with its own audit.

  While we're there вҖ” one more cheap win

  Line 106 of make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop:
  moho_gridy = min.(moho_gridy, partial_melt_gridy)

  The min.(...) broadcast allocates a fresh Vector{Float64} (toponum Г— 8 B).
  Since the result is reassigned to moho_gridy and moho_gridy was already a
  freshly-allocated array (returned from calculate_oceanic_moho), this can be
  in-place:

  moho_gridy .= min.(moho_gridy, partial_melt_gridy)

  One more allocation eliminated. Trivial change, fits the same edit.

  Summary of proposed plan

  1. Fractionation.jl вҖ” change calculate_oceanic_moho to take topo_gridx, 
  topo_gridy as args; remove its internal slice.
  2. Drainage.jl вҖ” change calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain to take
  topo_gridx, topo_gridy as args, return only top_mantle_partial_melt; remove
  internal slice.
  3. Fractionation.jl make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop вҖ” pass topo_gridx, 
  topo_gridy to both callees.
  4. Drainage.jl calculate_melt_drainage_divides! вҖ” slice topo_gridx, topo_gridy
   itself, pass to calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain, use topo_gridx
  directly for calculate_drainage_divides and the return.
  5. Fractionation.jl line 106 вҖ” moho_gridy = min.(...) вҶ’ moho_gridy .= 
  min.(...).

  After this change, equivalence verification will be:
  - The same drainage-divides integration test should still produce the exact
  expected [0.0, 18000.0, вҖҰ, 500000.0].
  - Direct call-site parity test (slice once vs slice three times вҖ” values are
  identical since gridt is read-only across these calls).

  Want me to apply this? If so, I'll do it as one atomic edit and re-run the
  tests.

вң» Cogitated for 1m 49s

  pass topo_gridx to it.

  Edit 1: calculate_oceanic_moho accepts topo_gridx and topo_gridy as arguments

                                                       в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
                                                        9 allocs

  вҳ… = recurring per timestep, scales with grid; вҖ  = small per-call.

  Per fractionation timestep budget:
  - toponum = 5000: ~320 KB allocated
  - toponum = 10000: ~640 KB allocated
  - Per 1000 timesteps: 320вҖ“640 MB cumulative GC pressure

  Smaller per-call than the marknum allocation we already killed, but recurring
  and on every fractionation call.

  Proposed plan

  I want to lay out everything I think is worth doing for this section, then you
   decide the cut. Tiered by impact and complexity.

  Tier 1 вҖ” High-impact, follows established Tier A patterns

  1.1 вҖ” Buffer-reuse tops and bottoms in calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt

  Add optional keyword args tops_buffer::Union{Vector{Float64}, Nothing} and
  bottoms_buffer::Union{Vector{Float64}, Nothing}. When provided, function
  writes into them and returns them; when nothing, falls back to the current
  zeros(Float64, xnum) allocation.

  New persistent buffers in model.topography.arrays:
  - layer_tops_buffer::TopoArray1DState (toponum-sized scratch)
  - layer_bottoms_buffer::TopoArray1DState (toponum-sized scratch)

  Buffers reused across both calls (oceanic_moho first, then drainage) since
  they don't coexist within a timestep.

  Update:
  - calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt signature
  - calculate_oceanic_moho and calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain to
  pass buffers
  - initialize_topo_arrays! to resize alongside compaction_array

  Eliminates: 4 xnum-sized allocations per fractionation call.

  Caller impact outside fractionation: 5 unmigrated callers of
  calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt continue to use the no-keyword fallback
  path (allocate as before). No behavior change for them.

  1.2 вҖ” Buffer-reuse smooth_surface

  Add smooth_surface!(out::Vector{Float64}, ytopo::Vector{Float64}; 
  nsmooth)::Vector{Float64} writing into out. Algorithmic constraint: out !== 
  ytopo because the smoother reads ytopo[iВұnsmooth] while writing out[i]. Caller
   must pre-allocate output.

  New persistent buffers in model.topography.arrays:
  - oceanic_moho_buffer::TopoArray1DState (toponum-sized вҖ” needs to persist
  through the marker loop because line 119 reads it)
  - partial_melt_buffer::TopoArray1DState (toponum-sized вҖ” also persists through
   the marker loop and is part of the function's return)

  Update:
  - Add smooth_surface! to SmoothSurface module
  - calculate_oceanic_moho returns reference to oceanic_moho_buffer after
  writing into it
  - calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain returns reference to
  partial_melt_buffer
  - initialize_topo_arrays! resize

  Eliminates: 2 xnum-sized allocations per fractionation call.

  Subtle correctness note for 1.2: the function used to return a fresh
  Vector{Float64}. After the change it returns a reference to a persistent
  buffer. If the caller modifies the returned vector, that modifies the buffer
  for the next call. In our code, line 107 does moho_gridy .= min.(moho_gridy, 
  partial_melt_gridy) вҖ” that mutates the oceanic_moho_buffer in-place. That's
  actually fine because each fractionation call rewrites the buffer contents
  from scratch via smooth_surface!. But this is an invariant worth documenting.

  Caller impact outside fractionation: all 7 other callers of smooth_surface
  continue to use the allocating original. No change for them.

  1.3 вҖ” Cache get_matids_oceanic_crust result on the model

  Currently vcats 8 small Vector{Int16}s every call. Materials don't change at
  runtime, so this is recomputing the same answer. Cache once at materials
  initialization in model.materials.dicts (or a similar permanent-state
  container).

  Update:
  - Materials initialization: compute and store the concatenated Vector{Int16}
  once
  - get_matids_oceanic_crust returns the cached vector

  Eliminates: 1 small allocation per fractionation call.

  Caller impact: any other caller of get_matids_oceanic_crust also benefits.
  Would need to grep them; probably a handful in melt-related code.

  Tier 2 вҖ” Moderate-impact, more invasive

  2.1 вҖ” Use views for topo_gridx and topo_gridy

  Replace gridt[1, :] with view(gridt, 1, :) in
  make_fractionated_gabbroic_magma_loop and calculate_melt_drainage_divides!.
  Eliminates the only remaining toponum-sized allocations in the hot path.

  Cascades signature changes from Vector{Float64} to AbstractVector{Float64} in:
  - linear_interp_bisection (MathTools.jl:201)
  - calculate_search_radius (TopAndBottom.jl:6)
  - calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt (TopAndBottom.jl, parameter gridx)
  - set_zero_values_to_topoy (Fractionation.jl:224)
  - set_zero_values_to_model_base (Drainage.jl:157)
  - calculate_drainage_divides (Drainage.jl, parameters)

  These are simple type-relaxation changes (just change Vector to
  AbstractVector); none of these functions mutate the gridx argument. Risk: some
   other caller may be relying on Vector{Float64} dispatch specifically вҖ” needs
  grep.

  Eliminates: 2 toponum-sized allocations per fractionation call.

  Note: would also benefit ~5 other places in the codebase that do gridt[1, :]
  (LavaFlowManager, RungeKutta, MarkerAdvection, CarbonateAdvect,
  UpdateSealevel) IF they're updated similarly. But that's beyond the
  fractionation scope you specified.

  Tier 3 вҖ” Cleanup (no perf change)

  3.1 вҖ” Delete dead calculate_moho in Fractionation.jl:167

  Verified unused; carries the old gridt[1, :] slicing pattern; small
  maintenance burden.

  3.2 вҖ” Reconcile duplicate smooth_surface definitions

  There are two вҖ” EarthBox.MathTools.smooth_surface (used only by
  HeatflowPlotsManager) and
  EarthBox.ModelStructureManager.SmoothSurface.smooth_surface (used by
  everything else). They have identical implementations. Worth picking one and
  deleting the other.

  Total impact comparison

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

  The toponum-scale memory floor cost from Tier 1 buffers is small. Compared to
  the marknum-scale marker_indices_layer buffer we already added, these are 3
  orders of magnitude smaller.

  My recommendation

  Tier 1 (1.1 + 1.2 + 1.3) is the right scope for one batch:
  - All three follow the same buffer-reuse pattern you've been using
  - Eliminates 7 of 9 remaining hot-path allocations
  - Low risk вҖ” non-fractionation callers fall back to the existing allocating
  path via the optional-keyword pattern
  - Verifiable via the existing drainage-divides integration test plus direct
  equivalence tests

  Tier 2.1 I'd hold off on for this batch. The signature cascade through
  linear_interp_bisection and friends touches more files and brings risk of
  dispatch surprises. Smaller marginal win (only 2 allocations remaining).
  Better as a separate, focused PR with its own audit.

  Tier 3 can ride along with Tier 1 since it's pure cleanup, no risk.

  If you approve Tier 1 + Tier 3, the change set is:
  - 4 new buffer fields in model.topography.arrays
  - New smooth_surface! variant
  - Cache field for oceanic-crust matid list
  - Updates to calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt, calculate_oceanic_moho,
  calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain, initialize_topo_arrays!
  - Delete dead calculate_moho, reconcile duplicate smooth_surface

  Post-change: hot path goes from 9 allocations to 2 (just the gridt[1, :] and
  gridt[2, :] slices, both intentional and at the top of the function).

  Want me to proceed with Tier 1 + Tier 3? Or a narrower subset?

  Correctness verification

  1. MeltDrainageDividesTest integration test вҖ” produces the exact expected
  [0.0, 18000.0, 84750.0, 150250.0, 215500.0, 281750.0, 348750.0, 416000.0, 
  483500.0, 500000.0]. Exercises calculate_top_of_mantle_partial_melt_domain
  end-to-end with all new buffers.
  2. Direct equivalence test вҖ” calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt with
  tops_buffer/bottoms_buffer/layer_index_buffer provided produces bit-identical
  tops and bottoms to the legacy no-keyword path on a 1M-marker, 200-grid stress
   test.
  3. smooth_surface! equivalence вҖ” produces identical output to allocating
  smooth_surface for nsmooth=5 and edge-case nsmooth=600 (larger than half the
  grid).
  4. smooth_surface! aliasing safety вҖ” assertion catches out === ytopo and
  raises AssertionError rather than silently corrupting.
  5. Cache equivalence вҖ” direct test on a constructed Materials shows the cached
   cached_oceanic_crust_ids after append! chain equals the original vcat result
  element-by-element. Empty before first call; populated after.

  Stokes build is now the single biggest contributor вҖ” and conveniently, it's
  also the most mechanically well-understood (we traced the exact allocations
  earlier).

  Concrete proposals

  Proposal B вҖ” Stokes build (highest impact)

  Targets the exact allocations I previously identified.

  B.1 вҖ” clean_non_zero_arrays! slicing (src/utils/BuildSysTools.jl:113-116)

  return SystemVectors(
      sv.Lii[1:nnz], sv.Ljj[1:nnz],
      sv.Li[1:nnz],  sv.Lj[1:nnz],  sv.Lv[1:nnz]
  )

  Each sv.X[1:nnz] allocates a fresh Vector of length nnz (tens of millions for
  Stokes problems). Five such allocations per Picard iteration.

  Strategy: keep an nnz counter alongside system_vectors and pass view(sv.Li, 
  1:nnz) etc. directly into sparse(...). Julia's sparse(I, J, V, m, n) accepts
  AbstractVector, so views work.

  Eliminates: 5 Г— nnz Г— 8B per Picard iteration. For nnz=30M, ~1.2 GB per
  iteration.

  Risk: moderate. Need to update every consumer of clean_non_zero_arrays!. The
  returned SystemVectors is currently passed to sparse(...); if any caller
  relies on owning the slices (e.g., mutating them), they'd be sharing storage
  with the source buffer. Audit needed.

  B.2 вҖ” Persistent SparseMatrixCSC
  (src/stokes_continuity_solver/.../SystemSolver.jl:33,
  src/heat_solver/.../SystemSolver.jl:40)

  Ls = sparse(Li, Lj, Lv, N, N)

  Allocates a fresh SparseMatrixCSC{Float64,Int64} per Picard iter. The CSC
  structure has colptr (N+1 Int64), rowval (nnz Int64), nzval (nnz Float64),
  plus internal sort buffers. Same order of magnitude as B.1.

  Strategy 1 (simpler, drops the symbolic-pattern-rebuild every call): once the
  sparsity pattern stabilizes (after first Picard iteration), reuse a persistent
   SparseMatrixCSC and overwrite nzval in place each subsequent solve. This
  requires stable pattern across Picard iterations within a timestep вҖ” likely
  true since the stencil doesn't change.

  Strategy 2 (Julia вүҘ1.9): use sparse! from SparseArrays to overwrite into a
  persistent CSC. Cleaner if Julia version permits.

  Either way, store the persistent matrix as
  model.stokes_continuity.arrays.Ls_buffer (or similar).

  Eliminates: ~3 Г— nnz Г— 8B per Picard iter (CSC arrays + sort buffers). For
  nnz=30M, ~720 MB per iter.

  Risk: medium-to-high. Sparse pattern reuse is tricky if the pattern actually
  changes between iterations (e.g., when plasticity nodes activate/deactivate).
  Need to verify or fall back to allocation if pattern differs.

  B.3 вҖ” MUMPS RHS persistent buffer
  (src/stokes_continuity_solver/.../SystemSolver.jl:36,
  src/heat_solver/.../SystemSolver.jl:44)

  R = copy(model....RHS.array)

  Vector{Float64} of size N per solve. ~5 MB on your case4 grid, called
  6вҖ“10Г—/timestep across Stokes + heat.

  Strategy: confirm MUMPS doesn't mutate R (likely true for the input vector вҖ”
  MUMPS computes the solution in a separate output). If so, drop the copy
  entirely. If MUMPS does mutate, preallocate a persistent R_buffer field and
  use copyto!.

  Eliminates: N Г— 8B per solve. Smaller than B.1/B.2 but trivial to implement.

  Risk: very low.

  Combined B impact: roughly half of the ~8.7 GB Stokes-build cumulative figure.
   Hard to be more precise without running, but should at least halve that
  section's per-call delta.

  Proposal C вҖ” Sediment transport compaction

  The 256 MB/call Г— 17 calls comes from
  apply_compaction_correction_for_topography_and_markers +
  decompact_new_sediment_and_compact_markers. Allocation hotspots:

  C.1 вҖ” calculate_top_and_bottom_of_swarm_opt
  (src/structure/utils/TopAndBottom.jl:205-253)

  Same pattern as the _layer_opt variant we already migrated:
  tops = fill(1e32, xnum)
  bottoms = fill(-1e32, xnum)
  ...
  if use_smoothing
      tops = smooth_surface(tops, nsmooth=nsmooth)   # fresh alloc
      bottoms = smooth_surface(bottoms, nsmooth=nsmooth)  # fresh alloc
  end

  Strategy: add the same tops_buffer/bottoms_buffer/smoothed_buffer keyword
  pattern. The compaction correction caller can use
  model.topography.arrays.layer_tops_buffer and layer_bottoms_buffer (the same
  buffers added in Tier 1.1, which are NOT in use during sediment transport вҖ”
  fractionation has already completed by then).

  Eliminates: 4 xnum-sized allocations + 2 smoothed allocations per compaction
  call.

  Risk: low. Mirrors the _layer_opt migration we already did and tested.

  C.2 вҖ” sticky_thickness_initial = bottom_sticky .- top_sticky
  (src/compaction/core/CompactionCorrection.jl:62)

  Broadcast allocates a fresh Vector{Float64}. Used downstream and discarded
  after the function returns.

  Strategy: add a sticky_thickness_buffer to topography arrays. In-place
  broadcast: sticky_thickness_buffer .= bottom_sticky .- top_sticky. Then pass
  the buffer instead of the broadcast result.

  Eliminates: 1 toponum-sized allocation.

  C.3 вҖ” decompact_transport_thickness_opt, compact_sediment_and_advect_markers! 
  internals

  Need to inspect. Likely contains marker-array-sized allocations for assigning
  topo_xindex per marker, plus a total_marker_compaction_displacement = 
  zeros(Float64, nmarkers) (which I saw earlier in MarkerCompaction.jl:725).
  Marker-sized allocations are the heaviest.

  Strategy: same buffer-reuse pattern. Sized to marknum, persistent. Need to
  investigate which exact buffers are needed.

  Risk: medium. Requires deeper code reading.

  Combined C impact: likely most of the ~4.4 GB sediment-transport figure. C.1 +
   C.2 are mechanical; C.3 is investigation-then-fix.

  Proposal D вҖ” Marker recycling

  +0.5 GB / 2 calls. Sources are 8+ small zeros(nrecycle_total) allocations
  across:
  - src/boundary_conditions/marker_recycle/utils/ResetMarkers.jl:18-20
  - src/boundary_conditions/marker_recycle/utils/FractureZoneProperties.jl:24-26
  - src/boundary_conditions/marker_recycle/utils/Coordinates.jl:82-83
  - Plus newx/newy zeros in marker_recycle/types/*.jl

  Strategy: preallocate a RecycleBuffers group sized to a reasonable upper bound
   for nrecycle_total (likely extension_velocity Г— timestep Г— 
  (nmarkers/domain_width)). Use views sized to actual nrecycle_total per call.

  Risk: medium. Need to bound the upper limit confidently to avoid undersized
  buffers.

  Combined D impact: ~0.5 GB.

  Proposal E вҖ” Melt solidification

  +1.2 GB / 2 calls is the same flavor as pre-fix melt extraction. Likely
  contains marker-sized allocations for melt fraction tracking, similar to the
  partial_melt_marker_indices pattern we already buffer-reused for extraction.

  Strategy: investigation first. Read
  src/melt_model/solidification/Solidification.jl to identify allocation
  hotspots. Likely fix follows the same buffer-reuse pattern.

  Risk: medium until investigation is done.

  Proposal F вҖ” Plasticity loop copy() calls (was Tier 1 originally)

  src/global_plasticity_loop/.../PlasticityLoopNodes.jl:111, 112, 119, 126, 134,
   143, 144 вҖ” six arr.array = copy(...) per Picard iteration. Plus
  update_nodes_for_plastic_yielding returning two fresh zeros(ynum, xnum) per
  iteration.

  We previously deprioritized this because it lives inside the Picard wrapper,
  which is dominated by the Stokes build (B above). But once B lands, the
  plasticity copies become more visible. Trivial change: arr.array = copy(x) вҶ’
  copyto!(arr.array, x).

  Risk: very low. Pattern-identical to prior commits.

  Combined F impact: ~0.8 GB cumulative.

  Cleanup items (low risk, can ride with any batch)

  - Delete unused calculate_moho in
  src/melt_model/fractionation/Fractionation.jl:167 (verified dead code).
  - Reconcile duplicate smooth_surface definitions (one in MathTools, one in
  SmoothSurface) вҖ” pick one and update HeatflowPlotsManager to use it.
  - Migrate the 5 unmigrated callers of calculate_top_and_bottom_of_layer_opt
  (structure/ModelStructureManager.jl:217, TopoFromMarkers.jl:56, 63,
  TopAndBottom.jl:33, Fractionation.jl:179) to use the buffer pattern. None are
  confirmed hot, but mechanically trivial once you're in the file.

  Recommended batching strategy

  Given testing is expensive, here's how I'd group:

  Batch B+F (mechanical, well-understood, biggest single hit)

  - Proposal B (Stokes build B.1 + B.2 + B.3)
  - Proposal F (plasticity loop copy вҶ’ copyto!)
  - Cleanup: delete dead calculate_moho, reconcile duplicate smooth_surface

  Total estimated savings: 6вҖ“8 GB cumulative (mostly B; F is a smaller bonus
  that fits the same change-review-test cycle).

  Risk: medium. B.2 (sparse pattern reuse) is the riskiest piece; if you want to
   be conservative, do B.1 + B.3 + F now and defer B.2 to its own batch.

  Batch C (sediment transport, second-biggest hit)

  - Proposal C.1 (swarm_opt buffer reuse вҖ” same pattern as _layer_opt we already
   did)
  - Proposal C.2 (in-place sticky thickness broadcast)
  - Proposal C.3 (compaction internals вҖ” needs investigation first)

  Total estimated savings: ~3вҖ“4 GB cumulative.

  Risk: low for C.1, low for C.2, medium for C.3. C.1 + C.2 alone is a
  self-contained sub-batch.

  Batch D+E (recycling + solidification, smaller but cleanup the long tail)

  - Proposal D (marker recycling buffer pool)
  - Proposal E (melt solidification вҖ” investigation first)

  Total estimated savings: ~1.5вҖ“2 GB cumulative.

  Risk: medium. Both need some investigation.

  My specific recommendation

  Do Batch B+F as the next single PR, but split B.2:

  1. Within Batch B+F, do B.1 (slicing вҶ’ views), B.3 (MUMPS RHS), and F 
  (plasticity copies) plus cleanup. All mechanical, all low risk.
  2. Save B.2 (sparse pattern reuse) for its own focused PR. It's the trickiest
  piece and worth extra care.
  3. After Batch B+F lands and tests pass, do Batch C as the next round.
  4. Batch D+E last.

  This sequencing maximizes savings per restart cycle while keeping each batch's
   risk surface manageable. Estimated cumulative savings after B.1 + B.3 + F:
  ~3вҖ“4 GB. After B.2 lands separately: another ~3вҖ“4 GB. After C: ~3вҖ“4 GB more.
  Working toward eliminating most of the 36 GB working-set climb we saw in the
  post-fix log.

  If you want maximum bang per restart and accept higher risk, B+F+C in one 
  batch is feasible вҖ” most of the changes follow patterns we've already
  validated. Risk is in B.2 (which I'd still recommend isolating) and C.3 (which
   needs investigation either way).

  Want me to proceed with B.1 + B.3 + F + cleanup as a batch (skipping B.2 for
  now)? Or pick a different combination?
